### Addressing Employee Requests:
Next, let's address Olivia's request for optimizing the SQL query to improve database performance. Here’s a detailed response, with recommendations for optimization strategies:

1. **Adding Indexes**: Ensure that indexes are created on the columns used in joins and the filtering condition (e.g., `trade_id`, `trade_date`, `sharpe_ratio`). This can significantly speed up query performance.

2. **Subquery Optimization**: Instead of using a subquery in the LEFT JOIN for risk metrics, consider using a Common Table Expression (CTE) or materialized view for improved performance, especially if those calculations can be pre-aggregated.

3. **Analyzing Execution Plan**: Use the database's execution plan capabilities to identify bottlenecks effectively and refine the query based on that analysis.

4. **Partitioning Data**: If your dataset is very large, consider partitioning the data based on `trade_date` to optimize performance for date range queries.

### Suggested SQL Query:
Here’s a revised version of Olivia's SQL query, integrating these suggestions:

```sql
WITH RiskMetrics AS (
    SELECT trade_id, 
        STRING_AGG(CONCAT(metric_name, ': ', value), '; ') as risk_metrics
    FROM risk_calculations
    GROUP BY trade_id
)
SELECT t.trade_id, t.symbol, p.position_size, s.strategy_name,
    r.risk_metrics, pm.name as portfolio_manager
FROM trades t
LEFT JOIN positions p ON t.trade_id = p.trade_id
LEFT JOIN strategies s ON p.strategy_id = s.strategy_id
LEFT JOIN RiskMetrics r ON t.trade_id = r.trade_id
LEFT JOIN portfolio_managers pm ON s.manager_id = pm.manager_id
WHERE t.trade_date BETWEEN '2023-01-01' AND '2023-12-31'
AND s.sharpe_ratio > 1.5
ORDER BY t.trade_date DESC;
```

Now, let's craft a response to Olivia with these recommendations.

### Addressing James's Request:
For James's optimization of the long-short equity portfolio using reinforcement learning, I will provide insights regarding the reward function he is trying to design, addressing his concerns about excessive trading.

### Key Points for James:
1. **Reward Function Design**:
   - While using the Sharpe ratio is common, consider switching to the **Sortino ratio**, as it focuses more on downside risk which may align better with your overall goals. The Calmar ratio can also be used as it inherently captures downside volatility while contextualizing returns.

2. **Handling Transaction Costs**:
   - Instead of applying a penalty based purely on turnover, consider including transaction costs directly in the reward function. This could mean calculating net returns after accounting for estimated transaction costs based on position size.

3. **Alternative Reward Calculation**:
   - A possible alternative could look like this:

   ```python
   reward = (returns.mean() - risk_free_rate) / downside_std - tc_penalty * turnover - transaction_cost * num_trades
   ```
   where `downside_std` refers to the standard deviation of returns below a threshold (the minimum acceptable return).

2. **Handling Memory Leaks**:
   - If you are seeing memory leaks and are currently using `Gc.finalise`, it may not be reliable enough. Introducing explicit finalizers for your C++ objects is a good practice to ensure there are no violations of memory management.
   - Consider using C++ destructors or custom deallocation functions to manage resource cleanup effectively.

3. **FPGA Implementation**: Implementing FPGA for order processing could provide the fastest option for execution since it allows for highly customized, low-latency processing.

Given the above options, the Equinix NY5 investment could offer a good balance between latency reduction and long-term operational efficiency.

3. **Wrist Stretch**: Extend one arm in front, palm up, and gently pull back on the fingers with the other hand for 15-30 seconds on each side.
4. **Seated Torso Twist**: While sitting, rotate your torso to the right, using your left hand on your right knee for support, holding for 15-30 seconds, then switch sides.
5. **Calf Raises**: Stand up and raise your heels off the floor, balancing on your toes. Hold for a moment before lowering back down, repeating for 10-15 reps.
6. **Desk Push-Ups**: Place your hands on your desk, walk your feet back, and perform several push-ups against the desk for upper body strength.

### Addressing Employee Requests:
Now, let’s focus on Sarah's request regarding the depreciation schedules for the new equipment purchases. Below are the calculations for the three items she mentioned:

#### 1. **Annual Depreciation for a $50,000 Server (Double-Declining Balance Method)**:
- **Cost**: $50,000
- **Salvage Value**: $5,000
- **Useful Life**: 5 years
- **Depreciation Rate**: (1 / Useful Life) × 2 = (1/5) × 2 = 40%

**Depreciation Schedule**:
- **Year 1**: $50,000 × 40% = $20,000 | Book Value: $50,000 - $20,000 = $30,000
- **Year 2**: $30,000 × 40% = $12,000 | Book Value: $30,000 - $12,000 = $18,000
- **Year 3**: $18,000 × 40% = $7,200 | Book Value: $18,000 - $7,200 = $10,800
- **Year 4**: $10,800 × 40% = $4,320 | Book Value: $10,800 - $4,320 = $6,480
- **Year 5**: $6,480 × 40% = $2,592 | Book Value: $6,480 - $2,592 = $3,888

#### 2. **Depreciation Schedule for a $200,000 AI Cluster (Sum-of-the-Years'-Digits Method)**:
- **Cost**: $200,000
- **Useful Life**: 7 years
- **Sum of Years**: 1 + 2 + 3 + 4 + 5 + 6 + 7 = 28

**Depreciation Schedule**:
- **Year 1**: ($200,000 × 7/28) = $50,000
- **Year 2**: ($200,000 × 6/28) = $42,857
- **Year 3**: ($200,000 × 5/28) = $35,714
- **Year 4**: ($200,000 × 4/28) = $28,571
- **Year 5**: ($200,000 × 3/28) = $21,429
- **Year 6**: ($200,000 × 2/28) = $14,286
- **Year 7**: ($200,000 × 1/28) = $7,143

#### 3. **Straight-Line Depreciation for Office Furniture Worth $30,000**:
- **Cost**: $30,000
- **Salvage Value**: $3,000
- **Useful Life**: 10 years
- **Annual Depreciation**: (Cost - Salvage Value) / Useful Life = ($30,000 - $3,000) / 10 = $2,700

**Depreciation Schedule**:
- **Years 1-10**: $2,700 per year
- **Book Value at End of Year 10**: $30,000 - ($2,700 × 10) = $3,000 (which is the salvage value).

#### 1. Sarah's Request on Machine Learning Model:

1. **Feature Selection and Engineering**: 
   - Start by evaluating the importance of each feature using techniques like Recursive Feature Elimination (RFE) or Feature Importance from tree-based models. Focus on market indicators, technical signals, and sentiment metrics that contribute most to prediction accuracy.
  
2. **Model Architecture**: 
   - For this problem, consider using **ensemble methods** such as Random Forests or Gradient Boosting Machines that can provide robust results and handle non-linear relationships.
   - If you opt for neural networks, ensure proper architecture design since they can model complex structures, though they may necessitate extensive computational resources.

3. **Handling Rare Regime Changes**: 
   - For the rare occurrences of regime changes in your dataset, consider implementing a weighting mechanism or anomaly detection algorithm to place more emphasis on recent data points that represent these changes.
  
4. **Evaluation Metrics**: 
   - Use metrics tailored for trading predictions, such as Precision and Recall in addition to the more traditional accuracy measures. Consider the Sharpe ratio or the Sortino ratio to understand risk-adjusted performance effectively.

#### 2. Zara's Request on Credit Strategy:
**Key Points to Address:**
1. **Switching to Hazard Rate Differentials**: 
   - Switching from z-scores to hazard rate differentials could provide better insights into relative value across CDS curves, especially in the context of assessing credit risks effectively.

2. **Addressing Illiquidity**: 
   - Monitor market conditions carefully during illiquid periods, and consider adjusting the entry and exit thresholds based on market depth or bid-ask spreads. With a typical bid/ask of 5bps, tightening the threshold may help curb false signals.

3. **Workspace Size**: Ensure the desk has ample space for your working materials, with enough surface area to accommodate monitors, keyboards, and related equipment.

4. **Top Brands to Consider**:
   - **Uplift Desk**: Highly adjustable and rated for stability.
   - **Flexispot**: Offers a good range of features at a competitive price.
   - **Vari Desk**: Known for user-friendliness with a solid design.
